--- Commit Message ---
LU-13798 llite: parallelize direct i/o issuance

Currently, the direct i/o code issues an i/o to a given
stripe, and then waits for that i/o to complete.  (This is
for i/os from a single process.)  This forces DIO to send
only one RPC at a time, serially.

In the case of multi-stripe files and larger i/os from
userspace, this means that i/o is serialized - so single
thread/single process direct i/o doesn't see any benefit
from the combination of extra stripes & larger i/os.

Using part of the AIO support, it is possible to move this
waiting up a level, so it happens after all the i/o is
issued.  (See LU-4198 for AIO support.)

This means we can issue many RPCs and then wait,
dramatically improving performance vs waiting for each RPC
serially.

This is referred to as 'parallel dio'.

Notes:
AIO is not supported on pipes, so we fall back to the old
sync behavior if the source or destination is a pipe.

Error handling is similar to buffered writes: We do not
wait for individual chunks, so we can get an error on an RPC
in the middle of an i/o.  The solution is to return an
error in this case, because we cannot know how many bytes
were written contiguously.  This is similar to buffered i/o
combined with fsync().

The performance improvement from this is dramatic, and
greater at larger sizes.

lfs setstripe -c 8 -S 4M .
mpirun -np 1  $IOR -w -r -t 64M -b 64G -o ./iorfile --posix.odirect
Without the patch:
write     764.85 MiB/s
read      682.87 MiB/s

With patch:
write     4030 MiB/s
read      4468  MiB/s

Patch Set 1:

(4 comments)

Patrick, what sort of workloads might cause problems for this patch, or by "error handling" are you thinking mostly of interrupted bulk, IO errors on the OST, etc?

--- Message (Patrick Farrell (personal), 2020-07-29 20:59:13.000000000) ---
Patch Set 4:

Andreas,

I haven't found time to read over Shaun's port of the patch, but my comments about error handling specifically referred to any error that would cause part of an i/o to fail (so, sure, an OST error, or even out of space).  Getting those errors back in clio isn't totally simple, and I specifically *did not* handle that correctly in the original patch, I left it for later.

Shaun,

If you fixed that, you'll want to update the commit message.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell (personal), 2020-07-29 21:01:50.000000000) ---
Patch Set 4:

As far as what would stress this...  I would want some tests playing games with stripe sizes and RPC sizes - Stripe sizes that are unusual fractions of RPC sizes and vice-versa, with i/o sizes that stress that a bit.

That's pretty much the only thing I can think of, other than adding an "is this working" test that would confirm we get multiple RPCs in flight.  (like, write 2M to a 2 stripes-on-one-OST file with 1M stripes, confirm that resulted in two RPCs in flight.  Note for that test to be reliable we'd have to delay commit/completion of the RPCs to be sure they're both in flight at the same time.  I specify a single OST because that way we can see they were both in flight *at the same time*.)

Patch Set 19:

Are we aware of any outstanding issues with ZFS and grant? :/. The reason that 398g test is failing on ZFS is because the client is running out of grant after doing just 4 MiB of i/o(!), then going to sync mode - which of course prevents getting 8 1 MiB RPCs in flight.

So, whether we know it or not, there seems to be an issue with ZFS and grant currently.

Patch Set 23:

Thanks - I'm actually going to have to adjust the tests...  I am getting write combining on the RPCs.  Sometimes a second extent is submitted before the first extent is picked up by a ptlrpc thread.

This is actually desirable behavior...  But I have to fix the test.  I will maybe put a fail loc to disable combining extents and use that...??  The problem then is two fail_locs in one test, so it can't work on a single node setup.  I will have to think about it a little.
